<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_de24f06d-05ac-4055-9b88-bf1cd2d6f8c0'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer14783832771870568447">This bundle includes Assassin’s Apprentice (book one), Royal Assassin (book two) and Assassin’s Quest (book three).<br/><br/>In a faraway land where members of the royal family are named for the virtues they embody, one young boy will become a walking enigma.<br/><br/>Born on the wrong side of the sheets, Fitz, son of Chivalry Farseer, is a royal bastard cast out into the world friendless and</span>
  <span id="freeText14783832771870568447" style="display:none">This bundle includes Assassin’s Apprentice (book one), Royal Assassin (book two) and Assassin’s Quest (book three).<br /><br />In a faraway land where members of the royal family are named for the virtues they embody, one young boy will become a walking enigma.<br /><br />Born on the wrong side of the sheets, Fitz, son of Chivalry Farseer, is a royal bastard cast out into the world friendless and lonely. Only his magical link with animals – the old art known as the Wit – gives him solace and companionship. But the Wit, if used too often, is a perilous magic, and one abhorred by the nobility.<br /><br />So when Fitz is finally adopted into the royal household, he must give up his old ways and embrace a new life of weaponry, scribing, courtly manners; and how to kill a man secretly, as he trains to become a royal assassin…<br /><br />Enter the extraordinary world of Robin Hobb’s magnificent Farseer Trilogy.</span>

    Why not? The entire story repeats itself again and again and again. Jealous, vicious, brutal, cruel villain, stupid, luckless, illogical ?hero (who, o<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Why not? The entire story repeats itself again and again and again. Jealous, vicious, brutal, cruel villain, stupid, luckless, illogical ?hero (who, of course, is deprived of his birthright). Oh, here we are again, more brutal torture and cruelty, ?hero somehow escapes, then gets caught again, for more torture ...... escapes again somehow, gets caught again, more brutal torture and cruelty, ?hero somehow escapes, then gets caught again, for more torture ...escapes again... gets caught again, more brutal torture and cruelty, ?hero somehow escapes, then gets caught again, for more torture ......<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_415314156" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/415314156" />
    <a title="Cha Pammit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8437282-cha-pammit"><img alt="Cha Pammit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1377683188p2/8437282.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/415314156?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cha Pammit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cha Pammit" href="/user/show/8437282-cha-pammit">Cha Pammit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer415314156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14853777156928300465">At first, I didn't know if I was going to love or hate this trilogy. The premise was definitely intriguing but I was initially annoyed at how the story wasn't going where I was expecting it to go. Fitz was supposed to be a gifted orphan boy who becomes a deadly assassin, dammit! How come he keeps failing at every turn! That's not the way fantasy stories are supposed to be written! The main character's supposed to be a hero with a few flaws like hubris or impulsiveness. He's not supposed to be co</span>
  <span id="freeText14853777156928300465" style="display:none">At first, I didn't know if I was going to love or hate this trilogy. The premise was definitely intriguing but I was initially annoyed at how the story wasn't going where I was expecting it to go. Fitz was supposed to be a gifted orphan boy who becomes a deadly assassin, dammit! How come he keeps failing at every turn! That's not the way fantasy stories are supposed to be written! The main character's supposed to be a hero with a few flaws like hubris or impulsiveness. He's not supposed to be completely helpless in situations and make erroneous decisions!! That's just stupid. And too... well, human. <br /><br />But then, by the end of Book 2, when Fitz starts recounting everything that has happened to him, confessing to all his "failures", lo and behold, a tear begins to fall down my cheek. And then two. And before I knew it, I was bawling my eyes out at 2am in the morning, cursing the unfairness of it all, and preparing to tear down anyone who dares to judge him for his mistakes. <br /><br />Little did I know it but the characters in this world have dug its way into my heart, firmly entrenched with no intention of leaving anytime soon. How the heck did that happen? Very sneaky, Robin Hobb. Very, very sneaky. I'm on the lookout for you. You won't take me by surprise again next time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14853777156928300465" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_686960277" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/686960277" />
    <a title="Justine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18656418-justine"><img alt="Justine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588653801p2/18656418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/686960277?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justine" href="/user/show/18656418-justine">Justine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22374216-the-farseer-trilogy-3-book-bundle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=2019-read">2019-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=favourites-2020">favourites-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer686960277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3430390996018511237"><b>Book 1 - Assassin's Apprentice - 5 stars</b><br/><br/>I absolutely loved this. I don't know what I was expecting, but I admit going into this a bit under-enthused. I know this first book is not overly long, but I've been feeling a bit daunted by long books lately (says the person who just before this read Stephen King's massively long <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6320534.Under_the_Dome' title='Under the Dome by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Under the Dome</a>). But, it was in part because I enjoyed Under the Dome so much that I decided I could still tackle big books without feeling bogged down. <br/><br/>Anyway. People have rave</span>
  <span id="freeText3430390996018511237" style="display:none"><b>Book 1 - Assassin's Apprentice - 5 stars</b><br /><br />I absolutely loved this. I don't know what I was expecting, but I admit going into this a bit under-enthused. I know this first book is not overly long, but I've been feeling a bit daunted by long books lately (says the person who just before this read Stephen King's massively long <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6320534.Under_the_Dome" title="Under the Dome by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Under the Dome</a>). But, it was in part because I enjoyed Under the Dome so much that I decided I could still tackle big books without feeling bogged down. <br /><br />Anyway. People have raved to me about Robin Hobb for years, and I'm glad I finally read this because it was so much better than I hoped for. I loved the depth of character development, and the slow and steady way the story was detailed up to that pretty fast finish at the end. Over the next few months I'm planning to read the rest of this trilogy, and I am now very much looking forward to that.<br /><br /><b>Book 2 - Royal Assassin - 5 stars </b><br /><br />This book picks up directly from Assassin's Apprentice, with things (as expected) continually going from bad to worse for Fitz. On the upside, we have a wolf!<br /><br />I was a bit reticent to start this only two days before the end of the year, but...I just loved the first book so much that I couldn't help but go on with things right away. Needless to say, I finished off this 675 page tome in those two days, making Royal Assassin my final read for 2019, and also my final add to my favourites-2019 shelf.<br /><br />Basically I loved this as much as the first. Loved the writing, the story, the characters, and the slow burn pace with the fast finish. It was all good and the perfect way to finish up the year.<br /><br /><b>Book 3 - Assassin's Quest - 5 stars</b><br /><br />So, notwithstanding all the travelling, which I know some people find tedious to read, I loved this book. I think reading the Farseer Trilogy books in succession was definitely the way to go, as all 2000 or so pages really do sit firmly in my mind as a single tale.<br /><br />Some (but definitely not all) favourite things from this final book:<br /><br />*Hobbs' treatment of PTSD and residual trauma. Wow, just so excellently done, not just for Fitz, but Kettricken, and all the characters who suffered so in the making of this story.<br /><br />*The relationship between Nighteyes and Fitz is an obvious highlight, and I love how it grows and changes. Nighteyes and his burgeoning personhood, as well as his growing relationships with others of his found family/pack was also a standout element for me.<br /><br />*The dragons! Ok, these were truly excellent. Their emergence was harrowing, emotional, and had me trying to decide whether I was pleased or horrified (both, really).<br /><br />Again Hobbs shows what a master she is at characterisation. If I have one complaint, it might be that Regal, while absolutely and truly horrible, is not quite as complicated as I might like. That's a minor complaint though in a huge cast of exceptionally well rendered players.<br /><br />Overall just so excellent. As a whole the Farseer Trilogy ranks among my all time favourites.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3430390996018511237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Groos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Groos" href="/user/show/40768714-paul-groos">Paul Groos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40768714-paul-groos?shelf=literature-and-novels">literature-and-novels</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1215331480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13722039520556867457">This is one of the few books of which I can't say why I didn't stop reading. It was utterly, mind-bogglingly boring. None (that is: not a single one) of the characters was interesting or even likable, except maybe the Fool. Everything (that's every single thing) the protagonist does goes wrong. Every time he might accomplish something he fails and fails again. The few times when he seemed to achieve something, it's revealed later that is went awry after all. The main, interesting mystery, the Re</span>
  <span id="freeText13722039520556867457" style="display:none">This is one of the few books of which I can't say why I didn't stop reading. It was utterly, mind-bogglingly boring. None (that is: not a single one) of the characters was interesting or even likable, except maybe the Fool. Everything (that's every single thing) the protagonist does goes wrong. Every time he might accomplish something he fails and fails again. The few times when he seemed to achieve something, it's revealed later that is went awry after all. The main, interesting mystery, the Red Ships and the "zombies" is never revealed. <br />Everything that everyone says is meant to be very profound. There is not a normal conversation in the book, no banter, no everyday language. Everyone speaks in deeply philosophical speech. <br />If there would be some action now and again it would help the story engage me, but each of the three books gets moving only at the very ending of the book. The rest is court-intrige within the walls of the castle. If done right, that might be interesting, except, it isn't. Waste of time and shelf-space.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13722039520556867457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer152434282597386861">Had been reading lots of science fiction and thought this would be a good break as it is a top rated fantasy trilogy. But it was a big let down. The pace was slogging and while the narrative was engaging, ultimately the character development and plot didn't deliver. Characters were actually named after their personality characteristics (Prince Verity, Prince Regal) which is as transparent as you can get and the antagonists was a sniveling prince that you thought would be dispatched by the first </span>
  <span id="freeText152434282597386861" style="display:none">Had been reading lots of science fiction and thought this would be a good break as it is a top rated fantasy trilogy. But it was a big let down. The pace was slogging and while the narrative was engaging, ultimately the character development and plot didn't deliver. Characters were actually named after their personality characteristics (Prince Verity, Prince Regal) which is as transparent as you can get and the antagonists was a sniveling prince that you thought would be dispatched by the first book but lingers on to the detriment of the whole storyline.</span>

<div id="review_1041482470" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1041482470" />
    <a title="John Chu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34491026-john-chu"><img alt="John Chu" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1041482470?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Chu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Chu" href="/user/show/34491026-john-chu">John Chu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1041482470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7807285042479174487">The best thing that can be said about this series is that Robin Hobb is a gifted writer, who has thoroughly researched and considered this world that she has created. The dialogue is clever, and the characters introduced are interesting with great backstories and are well developed. I also found the strong feminine characters, sprinkled in all unlikely roles to be amusing and interesting. <br/><br/>That being all said... the main character FitzChivalry is just about the whiniest, helpless, and most emotio</span>
  <span id="freeText7807285042479174487" style="display:none">The best thing that can be said about this series is that Robin Hobb is a gifted writer, who has thoroughly researched and considered this world that she has created. The dialogue is clever, and the characters introduced are interesting with great backstories and are well developed. I also found the strong feminine characters, sprinkled in all unlikely roles to be amusing and interesting. <br /><br />That being all said... the main character FitzChivalry is just about the whiniest, helpless, and most emotional character this side of the planet. For an assassin trained to kill people, he spends more time bemoaning his place in life and fate, than actually killing anyone of import. What he does kill, tends to be emotionless and feckless brainwashed character zombies. His emotions gets the better of him most of the time, and he can't seem to sit down to master any of the talents or skills, he's gifted with. He is a man (woman?) with premenstrual cramps 29 days out a month. His female compatriots on the other hand, are all strong champions of justice who seem to drag him along for the ride, while he wiles away his life drinking blackberry wine or elfbark tea and getting hangovers or nightmares. He can't assassinate or protect his king, he can't be a good father, he sucks at his magic, he's the quintessential fantasy deadbeat dad with a depressive/narcisstic complex who's place in this book seems only to be to bolster strong feminist zealotry and self-esteem for female readers.<br /><br />This series is 1 book of great narrative, and 2 books of whining, self loathing/depressive contemplation. I had read great reviews about this series and expected some high adventure, but I found this be mostly a character study, slog with repetitive themes of helplessness, self loathing, and lackadaisacal effort. Is it unique? Sure. Would I ever read it again? no.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7807285042479174487" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2077151394" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2077151394" />
    <a title="Laura Ardill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39451363-laura-ardill"><img alt="Laura Ardill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591169353p2/39451363.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2077151394?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Ardill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Ardill" href="/user/show/39451363-laura-ardill">Laura Ardill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22014069-the-complete-farseer-trilogy">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2077151394" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4185533183141483398">I stuck with this trilogy until halfway through the third book in the hopes that the protagonist would find some backbone and cease being an intolerable drip (he unfortunately, did not). The books are well written but paced extremely slowly. I'm a huge fan of The Liveship Traders trilogy also by Hobb and would highly recommend anyone who's interested in reading her work to give this initial trilogy a miss and start with the second instead, it's well worth a read. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_304422058" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/304422058" />
    <a title="My Awful Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7898542-my-awful-reviews"><img alt="My Awful Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1330058840p2/7898542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/304422058?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="My Awful Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="My Awful Reviews" href="/user/show/7898542-my-awful-reviews">My Awful Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer304422058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7864170786386647609">The Farseer Trilogy wasn't what I expected, and that's absolutely wonderful, because I expected something cliche.<br/><br/>The Farseer Trilogy stars Fitzchivalry, who at first seems to be a cardboard cutout of so many of the "poor farmer boys" from epic fantasy. But the drama, action and pain that he experiences through these three books is anything but typical. The Farseer Trilogy is the story of the red ship raiders that ravage Buck's coastline, using dark magic to turn those that survive their pillagin</span>
  <span id="freeText7864170786386647609" style="display:none">The Farseer Trilogy wasn't what I expected, and that's absolutely wonderful, because I expected something cliche.<br /><br />The Farseer Trilogy stars Fitzchivalry, who at first seems to be a cardboard cutout of so many of the "poor farmer boys" from epic fantasy. But the drama, action and pain that he experiences through these three books is anything but typical. The Farseer Trilogy is the story of the red ship raiders that ravage Buck's coastline, using dark magic to turn those that survive their pillaging into little more than animals, little more than zombies.<br /><br />It's also the story of Fitz's journey as a bastard child of the former King-in-Waiting, Chivalry, and the young boy's training as an assassin for the current monarch, King Shrewd.<br /><br />It's also a love story with an ending that is satisfying but depressing.<br /><br />It's also got dragons.<br /><br />These books were full of action, drama, and lots of painful scenes. Robin Hobb really knows how to give her characters hell, and it shows. Fitz is often very close to losing his life at any given moment, and has the kind of frequent brushes with death that reminded me of Harry Dresden in Changes. A lot of very bad stuff happens to Fitz, and you're there for every agonizing moment.<br /><br />This series is much closer to George R.R. Martin's A Song of Ice and Fire than I thought before reading it. What I mean by that is that bad things happen to good people, good people die, and sometimes the bad guy wins. That's not to say that they're horribly depressing, or so emotional that you won't be able to read them. Quite the opposite. You'll find yourself turning pages like a madman, because you're rooting for that idiot Fitz to figure out the plot and save the day, or himself.<br /><br />That reminds me that I need to mention my least favorite part of these books. Fitz is sometimes (okay, a lot of the time) a moron. Maybe I'm not a teenager, and for a good part of the series Fitz is, but some of the mistakes he made seemed pretty obvious to me, right up to the end of the novel. The information that people often tried to give him seemed easy for me to understand as well, but he just didn't get it.<br /><br />Despite Fitz sometimes being dumb as a box of rocks, the story is excellent, the descriptions beautiful, and the pacing of the plot wonderful. There were parts of the first book that slowed down a little too much for me, but once the tension ramped up starting at the end of book 1, even the slow scenes had that unmistakable sense of looming dread that keeps you reading and turning pages.<br /><br />I loved<br /><br /> Bad things happening to good people. This was real life, and sometimes life sucks even for the best of us.<br /><br /> The magic systems. They weren't very well defined, but in this case I think it helped, rather than hurt.<br /><br /> The ending of the series. It's sad, it's happy, it's perfect. I almost don't want to read her other books in this world, just so I can hold on to that feeling of perfect completion. Authors, take note. Hobb stuck the landing, and you would do well to study it.<br /><br />I hated<br /><br /> Fitz being such a moron. Come on, some of that stuff was pretty obvious, and he really should have been a little smarter about his decisions. I'll grant that he was a teenager, so that plays a part, but he still had me yelling at the book. I guess I didn't like it, but it was obviously good characterization to get me so riled up.<br /><br />The Farseer Trilogy gets a 9/10. Even with the glut of great fantasy, old and new, this deserves to be a series that everyone that wants to be familiar with the best the genre offers should read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7864170786386647609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_968590209" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/968590209" />
    <a title="Nerine Dorman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1611208-nerine-dorman"><img alt="Nerine Dorman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572964607p2/1611208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/968590209?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nerine Dorman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nerine Dorman" href="/user/show/1611208-nerine-dorman">Nerine Dorman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer968590209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13401268957759246140">Robin Hobb's The Farseer Trilogy numbers among the epic fantasy reads that I always intended to read again. Having read Assassin's Apprentice again, it's clear why her books are considered classics that you will find at almost every good bookstore.<br/><br/>What starts with the almost standard trope of the boy hero with royal parentage, is quickly subverted. Boy or Fitz as he is later known begins life as the unwanted, unexpected son of king-in-waiting Chivalry, and grows up in the stables then is later a</span>
  <span id="freeText13401268957759246140" style="display:none">Robin Hobb's The Farseer Trilogy numbers among the epic fantasy reads that I always intended to read again. Having read Assassin's Apprentice again, it's clear why her books are considered classics that you will find at almost every good bookstore.<br /><br />What starts with the almost standard trope of the boy hero with royal parentage, is quickly subverted. Boy or Fitz as he is later known begins life as the unwanted, unexpected son of king-in-waiting Chivalry, and grows up in the stables then is later apprenticed to the assassin Chade. <br /><br />He was born with the Wit, the ability to touch the minds of other living things, but if anyone were to discover this ability, he would certainly be put to death. <br /><br />The Six Duchies face an external threat from the Viking-like Red Ship Raiders, who devastate coastal settlements and leave survivors "forged" (magically violated and devoid of all empathy). Yet from the inside, there is strife. King Shrewd's son from his second marriage, Regal, has pretensions to the throne, and bears Fitz little love.<br /><br />Hobb has populated this saga with a rich cast of fascinating, diverse characters. Though the story is slow paced it is richly textured and it is all too easy to lose on self in the world she has created. I suspect this novel would have been released under the YA banner had it been written now, but Fitz comes to readers with a surprisingly mature voice.<br /><br />He really has a difficult time and his personality is such that readers can see that he has so much to offer others if only he had the opportunity to share his love. Due to circumstances he is a lonely child, however, and makes do with the scraps he is offered. He experiences much loss and cruelty yet he remains steadfast to his king. This is the redeeming aspect of a character some might find cause to despise because of his vocation.<br /><br />Hobb has it all in her writing: solid world building, ancient mystery, unforgettable characters, high adventure and enough courtly intrigue to give old GRRM a run for his money. I am looking forward to reading the rest in this series again. At least this time half the books won't be missing courtesy of our sorry library system.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13401268957759246140" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2012253135" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2012253135" />
    <a title="A P" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27909529-a-p"><img alt="A P" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2012253135?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A P" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A P" href="/user/show/27909529-a-p">A P</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2012253135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15432657708211824306">The story of dramatic teen angst!<br/><br/>The chaotically paced storyline hops all around but there is one thing that remains constant; no matter what happens and where things go - Fitz will end up neck deep in teen dramatic angst. <br/>Mollyyyyyy! <br/><br/>And it is not only Fitz who is prone to bouts of silly drama; pretty much everyone keeps taking their turns being a drama queen and sometimes (often) it crosses the border into the realm of unbelievable ridiculousness. <br/><br/>So many problems in this series. <br/><br/>-Protagonist </span>
  <span id="freeText15432657708211824306" style="display:none">The story of dramatic teen angst!<br /><br />The chaotically paced storyline hops all around but there is one thing that remains constant; no matter what happens and where things go - Fitz will end up neck deep in teen dramatic angst. <br />Mollyyyyyy! <br /><br />And it is not only Fitz who is prone to bouts of silly drama; pretty much everyone keeps taking their turns being a drama queen and sometimes (often) it crosses the border into the realm of unbelievable ridiculousness. <br /><br />So many problems in this series. <br /><br />-Protagonist who does very little to actually deserve that title. Most of the time Fitzy is sulking whiner and randomly does some blahblah heroic act. Other cast seems to consider him to be a hero, until they flip their opinion seemingly random or based on some stupid drama.<br />-Public opinion(s) that swings like a leaf in a tornado.<br />-World that makes no sense, most notably the nobility and economics. <br />-Antagonist whose sole role is to do antagonistic thing 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6; his antagonism and evilness is rubbed into our faces with every line that is written about him, yet, the world itself seems to be ignorant. <br />-Supervillain/antagonist who is supposed to be scary and dangerous, but seems like a random add on that is more ridiculous than everything... damn... his name is W*** (spoiler protection although prolly not needed)<br />-So many plot-duds! Seems like Hobb adds random sprouts that never actually mature. It's not that bad I guess, but so many and so random is bit... meh. Also, it kind of makes the first person narrator bit ... inconsistent? <br />-Most of the characters are unlikable, and more importantly, dull. Burrich and Shrew however do manage to break some molds every now and then. <br />-Contrivances (as always)<br /><br />Am not sure why I gave the second star or why I kept reading. Whatever it is, is worth that second star. <br /><br />EDIT: Going to remove the second star and give this one the one it deserves (imho). But just to mention if anyone ever even reads this one, Hobb also writes amazing books. ( I feel bit bad dissing a book with such fanbase ) <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1063279059" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1063279059" />
    <a title="Ryan Ailts" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3150837-ryan-ailts"><img alt="Ryan Ailts" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1330897009p2/3150837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1063279059?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan Ailts" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan Ailts" href="/user/show/3150837-ryan-ailts">Ryan Ailts</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1063279059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12290145881948544004">All finished and what a ride. I didn't expect to love these books so much.<br/><br/>I expected more typical fantasy and I got very little of that until the ending of the third book, which I swear was written in the 70s (in a good way) and sent forward in time. Other than a few types of "magic" that come into play every chapter or so, plus a dragon and some mindless not-undead people, it's very low fantasy. Think GRRM.<br/><br/>The characters are all unique and feel real, with the exception of the main villain, who </span>
  <span id="freeText12290145881948544004" style="display:none">All finished and what a ride. I didn't expect to love these books so much.<br /><br />I expected more typical fantasy and I got very little of that until the ending of the third book, which I swear was written in the 70s (in a good way) and sent forward in time. Other than a few types of "magic" that come into play every chapter or so, plus a dragon and some mindless not-undead people, it's very low fantasy. Think GRRM.<br /><br />The characters are all unique and feel real, with the exception of the main villain, who is a stereotype of the evil aristocrat, ambitious-no-matter-what. But even he has a few quirks, a bit of character history, to set him apart. His fate was not what I expected, but felt fair.<br /><br />Every person is treated fairly, even when they're not. How do I mean? They are written as human beings - every one has faults, quirks, moments they regret, the hero himself, Fitz, most of all. While he occasionally feels a bit Mary Suish at first, with how easily he becomes this beloved but still outcast character who is able to fix any situation and stumble into the solutions to all problems, as he grows up and becomes a teenager you see where his lucky breaks end and the hero, the human, has to come out. He whines, he overlooks things that hurt people he loves though we're screaming at the page to look, look, look. But he acts his age and pays for it. He ends fairly.<br /><br />I loved the books, mostly because of the emotional ride we went through with Fitz, the Fool, Molly, Burrich, Verity, Kettricken, Starling, Kettle, etc. I ended up dreaming about these people, unable to sleep until I finished the last pages.<br /><br />Great books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12290145881948544004" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6898501709168059386" style="display:none">I never read a book so depressing, lack of engaging action, hard to like characters, stupid and dumb protagonist, tedious/slow story line, and predictable plot. <div id="review_3032241498" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3032241498" />
    <a title="Shelly L" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38761322-shelly-l"><img alt="Shelly L" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551570094p2/38761322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3032241498?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly L" href="/user/show/38761322-shelly-l">Shelly L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22374216-the-farseer-trilogy-3-book-bundle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38761322-shelly-l?shelf=be_my_sci-fy">be_my_sci-fy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3032241498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3056403366926244651">Skillz, Hobb has them. For the first while, was swept away with this magical world, bonding as fully as one with a wit brother. Loved our boy, perhaps because he let us observe so much while saying so precious little. But then the first book ends! In a breathless rush of half-rememberings! And with the next book beckoning a kindle-click away, I flowed into the skillstream to slake my thirst. Questing out, into the raiding and the forging. The killing and the maiming. The tiresome lover’s quarrel</span>
  <span id="freeText3056403366926244651" style="display:none">Skillz, Hobb has them. For the first while, was swept away with this magical world, bonding as fully as one with a wit brother. Loved our boy, perhaps because he let us observe so much while saying so precious little. But then the first book ends! In a breathless rush of half-rememberings! And with the next book beckoning a kindle-click away, I flowed into the skillstream to slake my thirst. Questing out, into the raiding and the forging. The killing and the maiming. The tiresome lover’s quarrels and the teen temper tantrums and the obtusity. The excruciating abuse and torture, followed by the endless journeying and the traumatizing and the eventual, painstaking carving. Had to laugh when Hobb goes all Skywalker Ranch on us, inventing an animal in the third book, just because. One perfectly adapted to propel our plot, naturally! Well, but the plot is for the most part well wrought. Kept me intrigued, though at times, longing to give Fitz a swift kick. But I fiercely hated the bad guys’ dark deeds, and struggled with the good guys’ shades of gray. And loved our Fitz most of the time. And also loved well Burrich and Lady Patience and Chade and Verity and Kettricken and the Fool and Nighteyes, and even Molly, Molly, Molly. Though Hobb irritatingly disrespects her own creation, reducing our spirited girl to a tedious, whiny, “being a servant sucks so bad and your dick is the one thing that makes life worth living” status there for a second. Puhleaze. Ahh well, I forgive. The first book is magical, the second ends in pounding adventure plus satisfying twists and shadings, and the third starts strong with a fascinating tug-o-war betwixt wolf life and thug life. And the coarsening of a harsh-yet-humanistic society into one of rotten corruption and routine dehumanization is chillingly recognizable, my friends. Truly. Most of my gripes — tho by no means all — come of binge-reading a trilogy whilst wishing it were not one. My fickle feelings for series writing are well known, can’t be helped. And at the end of three, is it over? Not yet. For me yes, but for others, not yet.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3056403366926244651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_913677451" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/913677451" />
    <a title="Lady*M" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4751514-lady-m"><img alt="Lady*M" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294176460p2/4751514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/913677451?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady*M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady*M" href="/user/show/4751514-lady-m">Lady*M</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780007531486" href="/book/show/18904104-the-farseer-trilogy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4751514-lady-m?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer913677451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2911254803145021589"><b>Assassin's Apprentice - 3 stars</b><br/><br/>The book is a good introduction to Hobb's world and her main character Fitz. But, the pacing was problematic for me - from the veeery slow beginning to the rushed end. When the story remains squarely on Fitz's personal struggles, it's good. But, the magic system - Skill especially - was poorly explained and Fitz, even young as he is, accepts his fate almost without a doubt, which made me cranky. It was easy to tell who the bad guys were, so much so that I wondered </span>
  <span id="freeText2911254803145021589" style="display:none"><b>Assassin's Apprentice - 3 stars</b><br /><br />The book is a good introduction to Hobb's world and her main character Fitz. But, the pacing was problematic for me - from the veeery slow beginning to the rushed end. When the story remains squarely on Fitz's personal struggles, it's good. But, the magic system - Skill especially - was poorly explained and Fitz, even young as he is, accepts his fate almost without a doubt, which made me cranky. It was easy to tell who the bad guys were, so much so that I wondered how stupid the King and his followers had to be to miss it. Sooo, black &amp; white. The ending - with one bad guy disposed off easily, and the other somewhat cowed, but largely ignored - was a disappointment. The narration, in a form of Fitz's memoirs, robbed the book of some of its immediacy and therefore some of my involvement in the events.<br /><br />Hopefully, the rest of the trilogy would bring Fitz some growth. I liked the characters of Burrich, Verity and Chade. The Fool is puzzle.<br /><br /><b>Royal Assassin - 3.5 stars</b><br /><br />This rating is temporary, because, in truth, I don't know how to rate this book. I enjoyed it more than the first one. But, my enjoyment was diminished by characters' stupidity. No, not Fitz's. He is but a teenager often left to deal with the situations that require experience in the political intrigue, spying, military tactics. It is a wonder he does as well as he did. <br /><br />No, it is every other character - Verity, Shrewd, Chade, even Fool at times. People: If it looks like a duck, swims like a duck, and quacks like a duck, then it probably is a duck. How many times Regal has to betray for them to act? He is not brilliant. Yet, he succeeds at <i>everything</i>, simply because no one <i>acts</i>. It drove me crazy. The most intelligent person - for he is a person - is the wolf. The great 'romance' was tepid at best, Molly annoyed me for no other reason than existing. My bad. But, the time spend on romance could have been used for more natural introduction of Elderlings angle to the story. It's like Hobb twists and turn her characters any way it suits her - without giving them the proper motivation for their actions.<br /><br />I still enjoyed this more than the first novel. I want to know what happens to Fitz.<br /><br /><b>Assassin's Quest - 4 stars</b><br /><br />This is the book I liked the best and this is what the trilogy should have been from the beginning. I may wish for Fitz's destiny to be better, but for once - it was logical.<br /><br />I enjoyed both his travels with Nighteyes alone and with the rest of the group. We can see how he gradually matures. His bond with Nighteyes was great (and often funny) as the wolf assumed some of human traits. And, there is Fool. Lovely, lovely Fool. I enjoyed how his character was developed here. In fact, I enjoyed all the characters, even the annoying ones, lol. It seemed to me that the characters and events were developed naturally for the first time in the trilogy. The book has finally sold me the whole thing.<br /><br />The dragons were fantastic, duh.<br /><br /><b>Overall rating - 3.5 stars</b><br /><br />Final thoughts - while there were many things that I disliked, I am invested now in these characters so I'll read the Tawny Man Trilogy for sure... after a break.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2911254803145021589" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3426828504" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3426828504?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="anusha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="anusha" href="/user/show/28205345-anusha">anusha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22374216-the-farseer-trilogy-3-book-bundle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28205345-anusha?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3426828504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15562049092132859350"><b> “Fool, there is no sense in trying to play that game with the past. Here is where we are today, and we can only make our moves from here.” </b><br/><br/>The Farseer Trilogy by Robin Hobb, tells the story of Fitz, a royal bastard, and his struggle to be accepted in the nobility, despite his parentage. Fitz is groomed to be a royal assassin but he hides a more dangerous skill - the Wit, that is the ability to talk to animals, widely disfavoured by the royalty.<br/><br/>To Hobb’s credit, the premise is definitely intrigu</span>
  <span id="freeText15562049092132859350" style="display:none"><b> “Fool, there is no sense in trying to play that game with the past. Here is where we are today, and we can only make our moves from here.” </b><br /><br />The Farseer Trilogy by Robin Hobb, tells the story of Fitz, a royal bastard, and his struggle to be accepted in the nobility, despite his parentage. Fitz is groomed to be a royal assassin but he hides a more dangerous skill - the Wit, that is the ability to talk to animals, widely disfavoured by the royalty.<br /><br />To Hobb’s credit, the premise is definitely intriguing, and her world comes alive as we watch Fitz train to become an assassin, burdened as he is with insecurity, doubt and suspicion. He strikes up an unlikely friendship with the king’s Fool, and their dynamic has to be my favourite. <br /><br /><b> “A message is not delivered until it is understood.” </b><br /><br />This, for me, sums up the experience of this trilogy. Unfortunately, the plot only begins to come together at the end of the second book, and the trilogy was excruciatingly slow paced. While Hobb colours Fitz realistically, most of her other characters felt pretty one dimensional and unrelatable. Also, she brings out certain mysteries and builds them up, only to leave them hanging in the third book.<br /><br />I can understand why the Farseer Trilogy has gotten so many 5 star ratings. There are definitely facets brimming with originality and innovation. But, it was hard for me to read through 3 whole books, when large parts had no bearing on the plot and the writing just didn’t seem to flow. Maybe, this trilogy just wasn’t for me. *sighs*<br /><br />On a brighter note, the cover IS GORGEOUS. While I might have found the story disappointing, this is definitely one of my favouritest book covers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15562049092132859350" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/680762055" />
    <a title="Joshua" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15896229-joshua"><img alt="Joshua" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580414983p2/15896229.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/680762055?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joshua" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joshua" href="/user/show/15896229-joshua">Joshua</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15896229-joshua?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer680762055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13980586767487284765">This book is written inconsistently. It flows well in some parts and in others we get a tasteless retelling of events. One second you'll be reading a brilliant dialogue the next you read a short sentence about how the next month went. The author has a habit of telling you things instead of letting the reader discover them. While some telling is good it gets rather annoying to be told everything as if without the rehashing of facts you would be hopelessly lost. We go deep into the mind of fitzchi</span>
  <span id="freeText13980586767487284765" style="display:none">This book is written inconsistently. It flows well in some parts and in others we get a tasteless retelling of events. One second you'll be reading a brilliant dialogue the next you read a short sentence about how the next month went. The author has a habit of telling you things instead of letting the reader discover them. While some telling is good it gets rather annoying to be told everything as if without the rehashing of facts you would be hopelessly lost. We go deep into the mind of fitzchivalry. It's unfortunate that while the series sounds promising the content of the story somehow manages to come across as dull and unengaging. The coming of age of a court assassin who has magical abilities sounds like the type of book that you just won't be able to put down. I have. On three separate occasions I tried to get into this book. Reading just a chapter more here and there hoping for some tidbit of action or intrigue. Yet somehow even when what I imagine is supposed to be a poignant or powerful sequence appears I find it wanting. Imagine picking up a novel advertised as a sweeping journey only to find that it reads like a bland textbook in your least favorite class. Perhaps one day I'll truly be so starved for reading material that I'll pick this "vanilla ice cream in Willy Wonka's chocolate factory" novel back up and finish it. I doubt it. It's simply too boring to waste your time trying to see if you like it. The ratings in my personal opinion are very misleading in regards to this book. There are many more engaging novels with very similar plots that one can find easily. The coming of age assassin who is special trope is hardly a rare one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13980586767487284765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1741283919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8890703784077336226">This series had me really twisted. The writing is superb. Prosaic, well read, a world I really could feel. Even the characters overall had a rich and fullness you expect in any good series. <br/><br/>The but. <br/><br/>But I really. Really. REALLY, disliked the protagonist. He was always weak, always moping, always self centered. His character development was halted numerous times and he was never allowed externally or internally to overcome his flaws. He embraced weakness and ignored his strength. <br/><br/>It drove me bats</span>
  <span id="freeText8890703784077336226" style="display:none">This series had me really twisted. The writing is superb. Prosaic, well read, a world I really could feel. Even the characters overall had a rich and fullness you expect in any good series. <br /><br />The but. <br /><br />But I really. Really. REALLY, disliked the protagonist. He was always weak, always moping, always self centered. His character development was halted numerous times and he was never allowed externally or internally to overcome his flaws. He embraced weakness and ignored his strength. <br /><br />It drove me batshitcrazy. <br /><br />If Fitz had been a secondary character and another character the lead it'd have been fine. Much of the cast felt stronger, deeper, and more forthcoming developmentally than the main was.<br /><br />At the end of each book you think. This will be his moment, this crucible will make him understand. But it never was carried. Forever held back into a deep whining and self loathing. Ooooh MOLLLY. <br /><br />O.o<br /><br />I drove the whole series with a tinge of hope but it was never realized, not fully rewarded. The end few chapters felt like a glimmer of salvation but felt rushed against the length of the overall quest.<br /><br />Read this if you can handle a wet noodle of a protagonist against an amazing backdrop of characters and scenery. Avoid this if you get heartburn when character development is stunted every step of the way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8890703784077336226" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText15880162321428166192" style="display:none">The series was recommended by a friend, and at first, it annoyed me. <br /><br />Fitz was supposed to be our hero, magically gifted, intelligent ... He was supposed to grow into his power and win through just like in every other book.<br /><br />Instead, he was a flawed character, struggling to find his way, bungling his powers and his skills, losing battles and getting in trouble. Sometimes he wasn't likable and sometimes you loved him for his actions.<br /><br />In these kinds of novels, violence is frequently gratuitous and excessive, and while this world had it's fair share of death and gore and battles, we saw it through the eyes of our heros, tempered by their feelings and reactions to it.<br /><br />Despite being occasionally slow build steam, this world had unique magic, welld developed characters, and kept me hooked through three books. Well done!</span>

<div id="review_1219480213" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1219480213" />
    <a title="Ilias" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32087770-ilias"><img alt="Ilias" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551832809p2/32087770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1219480213?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ilias" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ilias" href="/user/show/32087770-ilias">Ilias</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer11331654890364869172">From the time I let a 6-year-old Fitz into my heart, I have been in love with this story. There was something about the birth of the young character of Fitz that has taken up residence in my heart and it feels as if we are 'bonded'.<br/><br/>This is a wonderful tale, but one that has taken a toll on my emotions. I think I have felt just about all of Fitz's pains and heartbreaks myself. The ending has left me a little bereft. While it was a good ending, I long for so much more for the character of Fitz.<br/><br/>All</span>
  <span id="freeText11331654890364869172" style="display:none">From the time I let a 6-year-old Fitz into my heart, I have been in love with this story. There was something about the birth of the young character of Fitz that has taken up residence in my heart and it feels as if we are 'bonded'.<br /><br />This is a wonderful tale, but one that has taken a toll on my emotions. I think I have felt just about all of Fitz's pains and heartbreaks myself. The ending has left me a little bereft. While it was a good ending, I long for so much more for the character of Fitz.<br /><br />All the characters in this tale are wonderful. Nighteyes certainly lightened things up along the way, and I love him.<br /><br />This is an amazing story and I have been lost in it for weeks as I travelled with every character following Robin Hobb's masterful storytelling.<br /><br />If you like adventure, intrigue, real emotions, friendships, trials &amp; tribulation and great love - and of course fantasy - then I recommend this trilogy to you.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2175945047" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2175945047" />
    <a title="Michael Rullo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7207720-michael-rullo"><img alt="Michael Rullo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583618427p2/7207720.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2175945047?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Rullo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Rullo" href="/user/show/7207720-michael-rullo">Michael Rullo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">lovers of traditional fantasy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7207720-michael-rullo?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2175945047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15881265426285525822">Since I read all three books before doing a review, I’m choosing to review The Farseer Trilogy by Robin Hobb, as a whole rather than each one individually. The titles in this series go in order as follows: Assassin’s Apprentice, Royal Assassin, and Assassin’s Quest. <br/><br/>Assassin’s Apprentice starts us off by telling us about a royal bastard, later named Fitz Chivalry Farseer. A great deal of the beginning of this book we see him being raised by his father’s right hand man, Burrich. While with Burric</span>
  <span id="freeText15881265426285525822" style="display:none">Since I read all three books before doing a review, I’m choosing to review The Farseer Trilogy by Robin Hobb, as a whole rather than each one individually. The titles in this series go in order as follows: Assassin’s Apprentice, Royal Assassin, and Assassin’s Quest. <br /><br />Assassin’s Apprentice starts us off by telling us about a royal bastard, later named Fitz Chivalry Farseer. A great deal of the beginning of this book we see him being raised by his father’s right hand man, Burrich. While with Burrich, Fitz stays out of the court and royal intrigue for the most part. Then the King takes him under his wing and we learn that he is to become the royal assassin. I don’t think I’m spoiling anything too much by telling you this, because I think the titles tell you most of that. <br /><br />For the first book, you get to know who the good guys are, who the bad guys are, and you learn a great deal about the protagonist. What I found was that this was the point at which I liked Fitz the most. Through the second and third books, you see him grow up and perform the duties required of him, but that’s not what makes him unlikeable to me. I couldn’t stand how he makes such stupid choices. Each one seeming worse than the last. <br /><br />Let me say, I love the story. I think the settings are great, the characters have depth, the magic systems are unique and interesting, but wow is Fitz disappointing. I read through these three books with such speed because I was desperately searching for results that just never come to pass. Eventually, the main antagonist gets dealt with in an interesting and suitable way, just not the way you’re hoping for the whole time. I will admit, even though Fitz could’ve dealt with him by the end of the first book, it would have ended the trilogy before it began. I enjoyed reading through all three books, so I’m glad that didn’t happen, there just isn’t a good explanation as to why it didn’t happen because it so easily could have. Maybe it’s just that hindsight is 20/20, and no one but the reader saw the results of this oversight coming, but it’s a little hard to believe.<br /><br />I don’t think this should stop you from reading through these books though. I think it was a choice the writer made to make her protagonist, and narrator, a rather unlikeable fellow. I don’t necessarily think it was the wisest choice, but I do believe it was a conscious one. It did drive me to read through all three books voraciously. I wanted to see Fitz make certain choices, I was lead to believe that he might, and then I wanted to scream when he didn’t. I kept reading though because I had to see what happened next. It was like watching the trainwreck that was Fitz Chivalry’s life, and I couldn’t look away. <br /><br />The first book introduces you to the character, to the world, to the rest of the players, and sets up the story. The second book shows the protagonist growing and getting stronger, and makes you feel like there’s no way he’s not going to lose, just to rip the rug out from under you. Then the third book shows you just how many ways a thing can go wrong, and leaves you guessing until the end how the good guys can possibly win. <br /><br />I would not recommend reading these unless you know you can read all three soon after each other. Trust me. I do recommend that you definitely read them though. If you are a fan of fantasy, if you like roguish characters, if you enjoy reading stories from a medieval-esque time period, and if you love dogs - yes, if you love dogs or if you consider wolves to be your spirit animals - then definitely read these books. <br /><br />Last but not least, I will make mention that this trilogy is the beginning of a series that Robin Hobb wrote made up of three more trilogies and one quartet, all set in the same universe. After this you have The Liveship Traders Trilogy, The Tawny Man Trilogy, The Rain Wild Chronicles (quartet), and the Fitz and the Fool Trilogy to read and indulge in. I only had access to the Farseer Trilogy for now, but I’m glad I read it, and can’t wait to continue on the rest of the journey in the realm of the elderlings! Come and join me! <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15881265426285525822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1186331851" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1186331851" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5488677-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326081924p2/5488677.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1186331851?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/5488677-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780804180597" href="/book/show/22479221-the-farseer-trilogy-3-book-bundle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1186331851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer963698835248947827">I was looking for a trilogy of 1990s-style (pre-Twilight, Hunger Games, Game of Thrones explosion) fantasy. One that was true to the genre with a few understated stereotypes and not too much predictability. This trilogy was exactly that. <br/><br/>ASSASIN'S APPRENTICE really sucked me in. Even though I don't generally like 1st person narration, Fitz told his story well in a (mostly) humble reflective voice that was easy to enjoy. The characters he interacts with are beautifully developed with strengths, w</span>
  <span id="freeText963698835248947827" style="display:none">I was looking for a trilogy of 1990s-style (pre-Twilight, Hunger Games, Game of Thrones explosion) fantasy. One that was true to the genre with a few understated stereotypes and not too much predictability. This trilogy was exactly that. <br /><br />ASSASIN'S APPRENTICE really sucked me in. Even though I don't generally like 1st person narration, Fitz told his story well in a (mostly) humble reflective voice that was easy to enjoy. The characters he interacts with are beautifully developed with strengths, weaknesses, and flaws on both sides of the story. I enjoyed every word of the first book. <br /><br />ROYAL ASSASSIN was a book with more meat to it. The characters are mostly known, and Fitz is growing up. He is finding his place in the world, learning about love and friendship, and trying to define who he is. His rivals start to become his enemies and he starts to gain some confidence. The story also takes a darker turn here as the challenges he will face make themselves known. <br /><br />ASSASSIN'S QUEST had a more emotional tone to it than the others. I confess that, in the beginning, I wasn't sure that I wanted to see where it would go because it started off so bleak. I made myself continue reading and was really glad I did. The final book in this trilogy doesn't disappoint. <br /><br />I love the way Robin Hobb treats her characters. She doesn't put them in difficult situations without reason. She let's them grow and change, and she doesn't pull her punches. It makes them all seem so alive. Even her minor charters have personalities and stories that make them interesting and unique. I look forward to reading more of her books in the future. If you consider yourself a fan of the fantasy genre, you must read some of her works. She truly is an amazing talent.</span>
  <a data-text-id="963698835248947827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Fitz Chivalry never got the easy end of things, and by the end I remember being exhausted, morose and emotionally drained. And sad.<br/>And thus I swore not to read the other Hobb books, not because they are not any good - because these are both fantastically written and quite imaginative, b</span>
  <span id="freeText9321974080427083750" style="display:none">I don't remember whether I have written individual reviews for these books so I thought might as well review them together.<br /><br />So first things first - this is the review of the original trilogy.<br /><br />And it was depressing. Martin</a>.<br /><br />(And yes I have found out that her latest book all ties it up, gives him back his heart's desire and gives him a happily ever after, but I am still not tempted)<br /><br />As a sidenote, I found the fool to be an absolutely delightful character especially in his(her?) ambiguity.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kC7XdngFTbfxaRX2HEz/IVp1Ajo34T1/jB7WZqpS2nUU6pD0decmhjAE3mHi8Kw9nZK4dHBrbeQYrEsU3phs4w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KZxTPRsjMcafklI6JQw5q+AaJ7V0+VscfSuyJ+68gpGtWBS/FsFa917/ma3bsGq3J/2d+zNzC4fpmS9VmnY0Bw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
